Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work until you have completed it; then look with your skill if there remain any small scrofulous lumps, cut them and clean the wound.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous lump, it is not appropriate to cut this scrofulous lump at its root, but rather tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall out without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment and treat it.[« Previous (3) | Next (1) »
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut out the entire abscess, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew it up, since there is no remaining excess due to the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you aim to cut out the root of it and pull it out, and sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For those abscesses that have excess matter, pierce them where they are swollen; and pierce it in the same way as previously described, by hanging down, then apply dressings with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with a dressing that draws out corrupt matter until it heals.
de squinance	The term "de squinance" in Old French can be translated to "of sciatica" in English. Sciatica refers to pain that affects the back, hip, and outer side of the leg caused by compression or irritation of the sciatic nerve.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient people spoke and wrote about the operation of the throat (or "tailleure de la gorge"), but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and this is what their writings say.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the slit in the throat called "epiglottis" be cleared; and this is not done with ease, because all the veins and the patient's windpipe are blocked by those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two glands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid suffocation which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Then, when we wish to split the epiglottis, it should be split below three or four circles, making a small slit across, between the two circles or according to the length of the slit in the syphax, not in the cartilage; and these places are suitable for splitting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and slender.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat to its full extent, then split the windpipe until it reaches the trachea ring; and avoid cutting any blood vessels if you see any, then cut the syphax as we have said; and this will be evident by the section of the tracheal rings that jump out from the broken part, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed where there is doubt of strangulation, bring together the two lips of the windpipe wound, and sew it all the way up without the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) says that this should not be done until the throat is completely choked up, and the patient is judged to be dying, and there is failure of breathing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then place a bandage on the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and thus they are kept from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it passes in 3 or 4 days. And then they command to sew up the wound and cure it, until it is cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a young woman took a knife and plunged it into her throat, cutting part of the muscles in the neck; and I was called to cure her, and I found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and knew well that it had not received any treatment or been properly cared for except for the throat, and the air was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried and sewed up the wound, and cured it until it healed; and nothing happened to the young woman except that she was hoarse of voice, and later returned to her normal state; for this reason, I say that in cutting the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 These abscesses are called "goiter hernias," and are large abscesses in the color of a lump, and are very common in women; and are according to two ways: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no malice.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental (goiter) is of two types, one resembling fat, and the other type resembling an abscess coming from an artery; and there is fear, and one should not operate to make an incision except in the one that is small, and prove and search the entire intrusion: if you find it like a normal lump, and it does not point to any vein, then cut it, just as one cuts fat, and pull out all its covering, if there is any; and search well early, and cure it appropriately, until it heals perfectly.
des nous	of the nails
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many forms are there, of which I will tell all the likenesses; and now it is appropriate that I say all the difference that is between dislocation and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that a dislocation is heat and fever holding, until the boiling has passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With dislocation there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like an abscess and becomes large; and there are two likenesses, either fatty or moist, and very colored as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the knot, that you first test and inquire about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", according to its form as it will appear in the chapter which follows.[*]
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the way to inquire into abscesses of dislocations is to take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth, so that you know the instrument has penetrated the core, according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intruder, and be careful not to let it burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs and forms a bulge, whatever color it may have, then lance it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the incision moisture does not come out, know that it is fat, then make an cross-shaped incision, and take tongs, and gently flay it from each side and place it on the shirt where it lies so that you can pull it out whole with the cloth; and if you cannot pull it out whole, then tear it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 For if anything remains, the tumor will return many times; and if some of it remains, and the blood bothers you, then apply corrosive powders to the wound, bind it up, and place a warm, soothing poultice on it, treating it with other cures until it is healed; and if the tumor is large, then cut the two edges of the wound and treat what festers in the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein cutting is against you or if it's another issue, hurry and apply a little vitriol powder, leaving it for 2 or 3 days until the wound becomes foul and the boiling of the blood subsides; then return to covering what remains of the new wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 See here the forms of intrusive instruments, and they are of three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one called "breb", and there are also of three types: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistula; and they are similar to the needles used to sew up wounds, and are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and are proven more effective for piercing the blackened tracts of fistula; and there are also of three types: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of leeches are of many similarities, as you can see here: large, medium, and small ones; and there are leeches that have two curves of three kinds; and there are leeches that have three curves, and they are also of three kinds; and there are leeches that have two curves, and leeches with a single curve only, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these [leeches] are sharp, and some of them cut only on one side, which is used for skinning the nails, so as not to cut the vein or nerve; and of the introductory ones, the eels are placed in strands, so that the patient does not notice at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one never uses them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the skin of fistulas, in this shape, to stop bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And sometimes the cautery is applied to the wound that heals well from veins and arteries, and other times in this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes, the nipples of certain men swell when they begin to become corrupt, to the point that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must do so according to the form of this line from b to g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 then remove the fat and apply medicine to the wound, filling it with good flesh, then bring the two lips of the wound together with stitches and cure it until it is healed; and if the nipple tilts downward and is soft due to its size as it often happens in women, make two incisions above in the shape of two similar splits; so that one holds to the other at the end of each one, such that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from this line b to g; then remove the skin that is between the two lips and remove the fat, and introduce what we have said about stitches and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood loss, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses in the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are types of hard scrofulous sores or they contain moisture.[*]
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Then those who contain moisture should have their hair cut in this manner, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply appropriate ointment to it until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, lance it as we have said for scrofula lancing, and if the wound becomes pus-filled again, apply a cautery as we have said before.[ \]
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When an artery is damaged and the skin above it is stuck down, swellings often occur, and the same happens when a vein becomes engorged and swells; this can be recognized when the swelling is long and deep, and feels hard to the touch. If it is due to a vein, the swelling will be round and superficial. It is foolish to cut into this swelling, especially when it is located under the nails, near joints, in the neck, or in many other places, and can be very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then it is necessary to avoid the iron cure, and also the one who is at the head should avoid it, and in the one who is swollen of artery let blood above the skin; then make an incision along the edges, and neatly separate the artery from the tissues, until it is uncovered; then place a needle underneath it, and make it penetrate to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in temples; then puncture the area between the two ties with an intromissive [instrument] until the blood within comes out, and let the abscess be released; then make the incision small enough for pus to drain, and when it is healed, cure it with a suitable ointment until it is cured; and if the abscess is due to the cutting of the vein, then stain your hand with what you can of the abscess onto all the skin, then insert the needle beneath the area you hold in your hand, and make it penetrate, and let there be a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then bind the abscess, as I have told you, with the tie of one of two parts to both sides of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads will come out, then insert another needle underneath all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and bind the threads in four places; then cut the abscess so that the excess comes out, then cut the excess skin and leave what is tied; then place a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then cure it with tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as an abscess can occur in the artery and vein, so too can an abscess form in nerves when they are injured or from excessive labor, and similar things.[INTRODUCING NEW TOPIC: ANATOMY OF THE HEART] Moult est bone chose de savoir la maniere et la complexion du chief du cuer et des ventricules, quar il nous fet entendre la nature dou cuer et sa complexion. Le chief du cuer est petit et ront, et a la grant partie espisse en son dedenz; et les venes qui vienent de divers membres del cors s’y assemblent et se partent maintes foiz, et del chief del cuer issient quatre granz artères. La premiere va el chief, la second al bras droit, la tierce au bras senestre, et la quart au col. Et sachiez que le chief du cuer est plus chaut et plus seich de tous les autres parties del cors; car il a nez et odorifanz de toutes coses qui vienent en li, ausi con fire fait odoriferous fumée por la grant chalor qu’il a. Et cest chief del cuer est le plus seich por ce que li esperis qui va par tout le cors va premierement en cel chief et l’eschaufe et le maintient toz jors; quar quant li esperis eschauffe le chief del cuer, il s’espand en touz les membres del cors.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more often in shoulders and hips and all places where there are joints, that is, abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it can be in several dispositions without pain; and when one presses hard on it, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but beneath the skin; and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor downward or upward, and the one that is in joints should not be covered with iron: perhaps it would cause contraction; and the one who is in the head or forehead makes the skin crack.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut into its root;
des grosses boces pendans	of large, dangling pieces (e.g. bones)
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes there are "thelul" in the abdomen and not elsewhere, and it is a disease called "funge" due to its resemblance to them, and it has fine roots and large excrements; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his abdomen that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were jagged, and moisture was constantly running from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six; and the operation in the incision consists of looking to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the "artelul" (possibly a type of discharge) is white and moist with fine roots; so use a large spatula to remove it, and have the fire cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in cutting, there often come large bursts of blood, and if the blood flow overcomes you, then hasten to the cauterizer; and if you see the patient fearful and terrified of the incision of iron, then take a well-made flax thread, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then bind it, and do not cease binding the flax thread until it cuts the artery, and this happens without causing pain; and if the roots are large, there is fear of cutting even through the belly, but you can well cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not grow back; then cure the wound, and be careful not to cut the vein which is of foxy color and poor sensation and has a milk-like appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	Because it is an abscess that has grown worse, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the abscess bursts open
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of a swelling comes from a cauterized wound or a split in an abscess, and it is located on the stomach and exits some of the intestines, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is in front, or from windiness; and if it is due to the rupture of the abscess and the exit of the intestine, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with diverse outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the bursting of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with one's fingers, it rises up and then returns, and perhaps it becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and after heavy work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and clearly visible when you press it with your hand, and do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess is large and hard, and fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the treatment is to see if the appearance is due to the blood of the artery or the vein or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 If you must leave the care (treatment).
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 Because there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the boil, you must instruct the patient to expose their throat, lie flat and straight, then gird yourself with a bandage around the belly; then command them to lie still between your hands, then go around the place you have designated for the entire spatula, then extend half of the abscess above on the large hook; then bind it tightly with a strong thread or a cord of firm silk, and loosen the new knot; then open the half of the abscess extended on the ligature, and insert your index finger, and seek the intestine; if you find it entangled in the ligature, release it, and put the intestine back inside the belly; and if you find the boil, grab it with the hook, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or the vein opposes you, go gently around, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, and put them crosswise in the hole you made when you pierced; then pull the abscess tight in four places on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it rots, and let the dead flesh fall away by itself; or cut it when it has become thin and rotten, then cure what needs to be cured, and cover the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as needed, and close the place.
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of chancre, and how one should work on it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure by iron; and we say that chancre worsens in the groin, and requires great caution in the cure, and the ancients said that when chancres are in a place where they can be scraped, such as chancres that are on the breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, and one should remove it completely when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, one must not approach it at all, for I have never cured anyone of it, nor has anyone ever cured it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once; then make him bleed if there is obvious congestion; then prepare the patient for the procedure; then throw your leeches on the chancre and remove all hairs from around it without leaving any behind; and let the blood flow freely, and clean the area well with your hand or some other object; and if the bleeding is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then cure the wound with other cures until it heals.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have previously said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only mentioning this; and one should not touch the iron in these two similarities: namely tympanites and hydrops ascites, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore, when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not help, look if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and relaxation of the belly and similar things; then do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt. And if you see the patient to be of strong virtue, and they have no other illness but dropsy only, and they are neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed thus: lift the patient up straight in your hands, and have the assistant press the belly by pushing the water towards the lowest part of the abdomen, then take a blunt instrument such as a spathulum according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be sharpened in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And let it be pointed, yet not so penetrating that it may reach the intestines when inserted, and not wound; then check if the dropsy has spread towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision above the swelling three finger-widths directly under the navel; and if it is due to disease of the liver, let your incision be on the left side of the swelling; and if it is due to spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lies on the incision so that superfluities do not run to the weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and insert it, and lift your hand to leave a space between the skin and the abscess as wide as a finger or more; then pierce the abscess until the space is reached, and this is the place of the water, then pull it out and insert this instrument of which this is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And is similar to a thin silver hook, and is made of light bronze or iron, and has a small hole in its lower part; and on one side, it has three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a feather quill, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes cut into the quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 And at the top is the aluminum piece, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it then descends onto the instrument; you will then empty half or a third of it, because if you empty more than necessary at that hour, perhaps the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he may fall unconscious, or he may approach death; but empty it according to the quantity of its virtue, and in accordance with what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and his pulses; then pull the instrument and hold back the water, and it is now held back by the cork that stops up the hole which I spoke of earlier, which you pierce in this manner; then begin again with the instrument the next day, if you see the patient enduring it, and draw off a small quantity of water; do this for several days, and take care not to overdo it until only a little water remains.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and leave too much water, cure it with sepulture or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and dye it with drink; and cure it with drying medicines until it is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the blocking of the penis.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Not at any time does a child born have no perforation in the penis, or the perforation is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 It is necessary for him to immediately pierce very delicately at each spatula according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 then place or insert a thin piece of sponge in the urethra, and bind and hold it in place for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug and let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out does not allow it to stay closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 If his urethra is narrow, then treat it with a sponge plug, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those whose urethra is not in its proper place are injured, because some are born with the urethral opening at the tip of the penis, which causes them to be unable to urinate unless they raise their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the exit, and this is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the procedure is as follows: the patient lies down on their back, then stretches out the head of the penis and holds it in a position like the width of a pen, so that the opening is in the middle as it should be; and be careful not to cause bleeding, which happens frequently, and if it occurs, stop the bleeding with a styptic and cure the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of the genital pustules
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these ulcers appear on the penis, and it is an ugly sight; and there are malignant and benign ones; so one should take them with a subtle lancet, and cut and clean them all, then put damp cotton with Egyptian ointment on it; then cure it with definitive ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the abscess is harmful, of putrid color and matter, you should apply a cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have lanced it, and if the abscess is on the shaft of the penis, with part of it beneath the skin and part outside, you should remove the one that is under the skin first; and when it has drained, heal the exterior part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Because when you heal it all at once, the head of the penis is not secure and may become pierced, leading to blackening and corruption on the penis and in the anus; you must remove everything that is blackened and corrupted, then apply a poultice of honey, flour, pomegranate bark, and vinegar, and continue treating it until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, moderate the moon cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery is useful for two conditions combined: namely, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you must insert a reed cane into the penis and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hairs are dried at the tip of the penis, which happens in those who have not been circumcised, or due to wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with a small scalpel until the ligament is loosened, and release the head of the penis completely from all sides; and if this is difficult to do, then you must scrape it with a spatula-like instrument along the ridge of the penis and the skin; then carefully separate them, and place a fine linen cloth soaked in cold water between them, so that it does not become wet again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds that involve the severing of continuity; nevertheless, when we perform this work willingly, and particularly in children, it is necessary that we do the best and easiest work for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not prescribe circumcision for their children, as they did not practice it in their law, and we only have what we have gained through experience.[Comment on the translation](https://you.com/create?text=Circumcision%20is%20not%20like%20other%20wounds%20that%20involve%20the%20severing%20of%20continuity%3B%20nevertheless,%20when%20we%20perform%20this%20work%20willingly,%20and%20particularly%20in%20children,%20it%20is%20necessary%20that%20we%20do%20the%20best%20and%20easiest%20work%20for%20their%20health.%0AI%20say%20that%20the%20ancients%20did%20not%20prescribe%20circumcision%20for%20their%20children,%20as%20they%20did%20not%20practice%20it%20in%20their%20law,%20and%20we%20only%20have%20what%20we%20have%20gained%20through%20experience.&source=youtube&query=line%20by%20line%20translation%20of%20old%20french%20text#)
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen that most masters and surgeons who perform circumcision do so with a lancet and forceps, using a single scalpel; the risk is that the heart may be affected as there are two layers of skin, and one might accidentally cut the top layer while leaving the bottom layer intact.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Either cover it up and the pain will be doubled, and there is no certainty of healing for the affected part; and during the cleansing of the nail, the iron may slip and ruin the operation, and often times it happens that it does not require cleansing and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	I have found through experience that the incision made with force to the entire tendon of sinew is good, for the incisions cut precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you press your hand, cut evenly in the shape of an "I" all the while; but let the thread be tightly wrapped around the skin; and the first part of the procedure is to make the child, if they are aware, think that you are only tying the thread around the member, and then cheer them up in every way possible; then place it directly between your hands and apply pressure between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the member and blow or cough, and pull it upwards until the head of the member is inside; then clean it well of the filth that has accumulated, then bind the area with a double thread, then bind it below the opening with another ligature; and hold it for two days by the second ligature at the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two ligatures, then quickly lift the scrotum and pull the head of the member out; then let the sac fill with blood, for this is healthy; and put powder on it and on the powder a piece of cloth glued with half a beaten egg white, tempered with rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forceps for cleaning is as follows: the two ends should be sharp and should be of equal length, and the ends should be as long as the width of a hand.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleaning is when the kernel within flees to the incision; then it is necessary that you stretch it to your fingernail, so that the place forms an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with tongs, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it goes beyond three days, and what is beneath the foreskin is swollen, then let it be until the abscess has calmed down, and then gently flay it; cut as much as you can move without injuring the penis in any way.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat therefore the wound of burning objects with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if it boils over excessively, it will not harm; treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	of urine retention
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The holding of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, congealed blood, pus, charred flesh, or similar things, as we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see retention due to the stone that is in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should bend over their knees; and their feet should be placed on their back, and their belly should be extended from above towards the back, and the patient should strain their abdominal muscles as much as they can; and then the neck of the bladder is constricted for the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the instrument called "siringue", of which this is the form: and be made of thin and light silver, like the feathers of a bird; and let the cane be one palm and a half long, and be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of urine retention is as follows: take a double thread, and tie one end to the head of a wool or cotton cloth, and insert the head of the thread inside the syringe; cut off the excess wool and push it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a seat, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil, and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis over the bulge; then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and have the patient feel it come to the empty place, and this is not done in this order except for the fact that the conduit through which it passes is twisted; then pull the thread out with all the wool, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and let the urine flow; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and relieve the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scrapes or blood appear in the bladder, or putrefaction has gathered there, and you wish to distill waters and medicines inside it, do so with all the instrument called "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see; and the shaved area where the medicine syringe should be such that it effectively stops the nozzle, allowing for the removal of moisture and insertion when necessary; and when you see your medicines being injected into the bladder, place the tip of the syringe in the moisture, and pull the plunger; this will draw the moisture into the syringe, and then strongly push the plunger back in; this will cause the moisture to enter, reaching the bladder immediately, such that the patient will feel it; and this is the subtle form of an enema used to cleanse the bladder: here it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or brass, and the head (noisemaker/enema tip) is higher up; and below is the bladder where the mixture falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture (mixture) that you want to use to fill the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a strong double thread, and heat the pouch containing the moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the rectum, then strain your hand on the bladder until all the mixture has entered, so that the patient feels that the mixture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then put a strong string through these holes, then gather the circle like a drawstring bag, and put inside what you want of oil and mixture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do the same as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	The sentence "et met dedens ceu que tu vues d'oile et de moistor et d'aigue, et le lie en l'estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la piere." can be translated to:
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division the ways of treating stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between a wandering stone in the kidneys, and all its signs, and in which stones one should operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stones which are stuck in the bladder happen more often to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similar to water in its subtlety; and there is sand, and the patient urinates frequently, and the urine is thick, and then it solidifies; and for many of these, the foundation is weak; and the healing is light for children until they are 4 years old, and it is very difficult for the elderly, and it is of medium difficulty for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary to first cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and raise them up, tilting and moving them downward, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and comes out at times; then have him sit between your hands, arranged in this manner, with his hands beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downward; then search for it and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in this area, then hurry to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall by touching it all over, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adolescent; and insert it into its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull on the collar of the bladder; then press with your finger, and push it out where you wish to make the incision.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to lift upwards with his right hand the hips, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the hips in the area where the incision is made; then insert the spatula cutting edge, which is its form.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And make an incision between what is between the hips and the anus, not in the middle but to the left side of the anus; and let it be straight above the stone, and your hands should always be on the foundation or the anus, and let the cut of the incision be wide outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, and not too large; perhaps by pressing with the finger that is in the anus, it will jump out without difficulty; and know that there are some stones that have angles and edges: they are difficult to come out; and some are swollen, similar to a gland, and round, from which the extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Then at that place where there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump out, you must pull with pincers that are like a file at the top, to extract the stone so that it doesn't shatter; or you insert beneath it a thin curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot deceive it in this way, then widen the opening a little, and if the flesh is thick, constrict it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first put in the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cover over, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterward if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, you must saw it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or urine repeatedly comes out from the wound so that the wound cannot heal; yet you should make an effort to draw it out, or break it with tongs, as much as you can pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place on it a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to appease the hot abscess; then turn the patient onto their side, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, rinse the wound well with oil and water, then clean it with a fine ointment and a basilicon ointment until it is healed.[Answer 1:
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if pus or gangrene comes in the wound and solidification of blood in the bladder, and urine is retained in such a way that it comes out with difficulty: then put your finger in the wound and draw out that blood, for if it remains there, it will corrupt the bladder and cause it to rot; then cleanse the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help him in all ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that during all the hours that you care for him, you bind his two thighs together and apply the medicines on the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small, and it is located in the bladder, and lodged inside, and the urine cannot exit; then heal it as I have said before, that you cut it many times, it is excused from cutting for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have proven it to be so.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a fork of iron in this shape and let it be fixed with three prongs in one handle.[FADE OUT.]
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a thread and tie it around the bladder below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the probe into the bladder until it reaches the stone; and turn the probe in your hand within the stone, pushing and pushing, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then the urine will come out quickly; then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the bladder.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Is immediately broken, and exits with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any hindering reason, then tie a thread below the stone and another above, then place the rod next to the stone between the two ligaments, then pull it out, and untie the knot, and clean the coagulated blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women (possibly referring to a medical condition related to the female reproductive system, such as gallstones or kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is inserted in women, and if it ever occurs, the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled woman who exposes herself to physicians, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is that perhaps a woman skilled in this art of hands cannot be found; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper than that of the man, therefore a deeper incision is required, and there is great fear.
