Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this blockage is caused by a sudden closing of a wound or an abscess; in that case, it should be covered and treated, as we have said with the piece of wood.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the rectum (or: of the anus)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from under the buttocks are hard lumps, and grow near the buttock or in the space of two parts, whether it is one fistula or multiple; and when this hard lump is old, it works, and still has whitish moisture or thin pus, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are known by what comes out or windiness when the patient makes excretion, and perhaps a worm comes out in his stool.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and they extend to the joint of the thigh, and to the navel of the cow.[Note: The translation of "nout de la kowe" is uncertain as it is unclear what body part "kowe" refers to. It could also be translated as "navel of the calf".]
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And so one recognizes the persistent fistula in the buttocks, and not persistent: and it is done by inserting your index finger into the buttocks, and inserting a thin needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 And if there is curvature, insert a thin tent of linen or horsehair until you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no purging or wind escapes from the opening as we have said: know that it has not pierced; then hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has penetrated to the bladder or to the conduit of urine, if urine leaks out and it cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it [the tent] reaches all the way to the joint of the thigh, then the tent has reached its place; if there is no curvature and the cause of pain is not around it, then it is that it [the afflicted part] will always be bowed, and neither medicine nor surgery through ointment is of any use; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and foolishness from false practitioners who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In the one who is not persian nor ancient, there is hope of health through cure by fire, as I have tested; and let the patient lie with you, in your hands, on their back; and lift the legs up to the thighs, and have the thighs inclined towards the abdomen; then insert a tent of iron, or of wood if there is curvature, until you know where the tent comes to.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the anus, then you should insert your index finger, and if you feel that the tent has pierced it; and uncover where you feel between your finger the abscess or flesh, then know that it is persian; and do not work further on it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 Always keep in mind that one can indeed heal some [people], but it happens rarely; and the help that one provides is to heat the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and insert it very hot into the fistula until it reaches the base; and do this twice or three times, until you are certain that the damaged cartilages, which resemble a bird's feather, have burned away; and then cure it with moist bandages smeared with butter, until the remaining cartilage comes out; then cure it with a healing ointment that promotes the growth of flesh and heals.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If it is healed in this way, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If this [condition] cannot be healed otherwise; and if it swells and does not burst until it reaches the finger that is at the base, and between your finger and the swelling there is a thick covering of flesh or tissue; and you see the fistula following the cover of the wound; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the swelling forward, and cauterize afterward, until you reach the tip of the swelling; and the swelling will be released, and it will fall off; then clean away the decayed flesh, which looks like a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood overpowers you and flows between you and the procedure, cauterize it with fire or a medicinal styptic.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 For the fire cautery brings about two good things: namely, the burning away of joined flesh and the stopping of blood and the drying up of moisture; then the treatment of wet swellings with butter or crushed herbs, until the place softens and the burned flesh comes out in the softened area; then heal the wound with drying remedies for suppurating hard flesh, and they are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the depth of the fundament, and is removed from the body, place your finger in the opening and feel it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the abscess, and between two are the cloth or syringe or knife, close to piercing, let there be no fear but rather hope and confidence through the administration of one of three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it down to the base, or if possible, you place tents and cure it as before; and do not go too deep, so as not to cut the support that holds the foundation, and let the pus come out willingly; then cure it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it once it has been cut next to the foundation, either with a tent or with some other pointed instrument; then clean the cavity that is in the wound, as much as you can; then strive to restore the wound and keep the fistula on the outside of the foundation: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fistulas are formed in this way: when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is next to the base near the skin above, take a probe pierced at the tip in this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a twisted wire through (the hole of) the two (prongs), and push the tent peg all the way to the top of the fistula.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it (the probe) is pierced in the margin of the base inside, then pull out the thread from that hole, as you insert your finger into the base; and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two sides together, and hold them close to each other, and leave it for one day or two; and tighten it occasionally, until the threads cut through the flesh between them and fall out; then cure the wound until it heals and becomes clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because one should not at all make the incision cover so deeply and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The shape of the spine-handled syringe with which one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	"of hemorrhoids"
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Piles are of two types: either they are inside the anus, like a grain of resin, and these can be small or large, and cause bleeding, and there can be one or more, and they are under or at the base of the anus; but those that are outside have little moisture, and still sometimes contain yellow water or blood, and have the color of flesh. And the treatment for those who have them inside is that you instruct the patient to strain when going to the bathroom, so that the anus protrudes and the threads appear; then hurry and use pincers or hold it with your fingernail, and cut it at its roots. And if the hooks cannot be held because of their moisture, take them with a piece of cloth or cotton or a piece of chamois leather, and pull them out with your hands, then cut them, and sprinkle hot powders on them instead of cauterizing; or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, and cure them with other cures until they are healed. And if the anus cannot come out, enema the patient with a bitter and harsh enema to clean what is in the anus, so that it can come out openly. When the patient feels the urge, and the threads have come out of the anus, the cure is easy; and it is that you take them with your fingernail or pincers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said until they are healed, and make sure the incision by iron is feared.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 You should prepare the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread above and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle, and let it be of suitable width; pull the thread tight, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same for all the others, and leave one to correct the excess blood; then place a wet cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote on the wound, and place it on the wound, and instruct the patient to rest; and let it be so until he/she urinates, and when they have fallen off, cure them with ointment and other cures, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	with drying of pus or wound.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It often happens that there is drying of pus in the intestines, due to constrictions of nature, and when the illness is old and no medicine helps.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary that you place the bark of a spatula or your nail on it, preventing it from getting moist; then heal it until it is solid as it should be; and if it cannot solidify, repeat the shaving more forcefully than before, so that it heals well and is scraped; then heal it until it is healed.
dou fremit	shivering[INT] de fièvre et de froit
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A formica (ant) is a small, hollow appearance in the body, going very deep; and sometimes it is found, and it feels like the dead skin of gooseflesh, and spreads throughout the body, more so in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure is to take a quill from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather, and place that quill on the gooseflesh, until the circle encompasses the gooseflesh all around; then turn your hand around the entire quill, so you scrape all around the gooseflesh, and push it in deep, and extract the gooseflesh from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a reed of iron or steel in this manner, and make it fine underneath and drawing upwards:[INT](Note: I noticed that there are no line breaks in the original text. Here I will add them to make it easier to read.)
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Not too deeply, in order to hold it with the finger, and press gently
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the enema syringe
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	An enema is never made with a silver or copper syringe, or with melted tin or iron; and sometimes they are made with these instruments, large or small, depending on who they are prepared for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those who are used in the care of children and infirm adults are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large enema syringe is broad at the top, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And there is a dislocation where the belly is bound, as you see, and the anus is pierced inside; and has two openings on one side, and one on the other; and let the belly be a place where medicines from an animal bladder or parchment are put, and let it be pierced all around with small holes, and have between each hole 1 digit of space, then insert a strong thread of twisted silk in X or around it, and bind the belly as if it were a sack; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then perform an enema; and this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or similar thing, then insert it gently; then the minister should press it with both hands until it is completely inside, then remove the enema, and raise the patient's legs in the air, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as much as it can; and if he sleeps a whole night, it will be a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema to a patient with a disorder of the belly, and the medicine quickly comes out, re-administer it until it is clear that it has taken effect.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if there are piles or a abscess on the fundament, let the enema be as fine as for a child; and this is the shape of the fine enema, where the leather is stretched:
des plaies	from wounds[STHAPPY]
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have previously said in the division the cure for wounds; now we will tell you the cures for hands and remedies, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are: striking of a stone, cutting by a sword and knife, or by a lance or stick or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound falling on the neck, or head, or chest, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, for memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is due to a blow from a stone or similar things, and the skin is torn and the wound is large, and you suspect a hot abscess: then have it cauterized immediately from the same head if there is little bleeding from the wound, and let the incision be contrary to the injured part; and make the patient empty themselves of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he does not want to be cauterized, then let his food be reduced, and let him not drink wine, nor eat meat or any other solid food; and put on the wound, if a hot abscess is suspected, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, but it is a fresh wound with all its blood, and it has not been exposed to air, then put on a powder which I will mention later; and if the wound has been exposed to air, then put on some remedies until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a cut from a sword or similar, and the lips cannot come together with bandages, then bring them together with stitches, as I will say for wounds of the belly, through stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed to the bone, and is festering and only holds together by a small amount, then cut it; after that, cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat solid foods, such as meat and cooked wheat, also poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find rotten flesh on the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, then cut away all the rotten flesh and discard it, then cure the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound or a vein, which cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if the wounds are small and simple, then the cure is easy: which is to apply this powder that coagulates once the arrow has moved it.[NOTE: I'm assuming "ars" is a typo and should be "aros" (arrows).]
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it dries out and joins with all its blood; and then bind it securely, and leave it unbound if it does not swell; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with lime alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but the physician has dried out the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound has been infected by matter, even in this case, do not put this powder on it at all; but apply some digestive ointments or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey until it dries out; then treat it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the fracture of bones comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate forceps; and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	about the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, except if the sinew or artery of the neck is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerve, there is no other remedy but to leave the wound alone and not apply anything restricting, for that harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not place anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as lime washed in clean water, and mixed with rose oil, and also wash the cubebs in clean water, and other similar stones in this manner, and use moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, let it be sewn and bandaged, and leave it to heal until it is healed.[ST1]
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and jagged and filled with flesh debris, pierce it lower at a different spot; and if an artery is cut and bleeding occurs, tie it off, stitch it up, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat or windpipe is cut and the conduit that allows food is preserved, place the windpipe on the groove of the throat, but do not let it touch the throat and return it to its natural figure; and then bind it appropriately, leaving it for some days, and cure it with discarded salves until it heals; and if the wound has left an impression on the bone, seek it out; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them all out if you can, and what you cannot, leave until the wound rots, and the opening discharges and heals; and if the wound is fresh, apply powder as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is also a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a spear or knife blow, and the wound is deep, look if air escapes from the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it immediately, nor bind it so that the blood does not clot deeply and returns to the heart, causing the patient to die quickly; but put attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more; no spasms or bad tremors of the heart or constrictions of the breath will come, and when you see good signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Cure then the abscess and other wounds, until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and produces pus, know that there is a fistula; so cure it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the belly side or back, cure what is in front; if it is large, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is close to the bone, and has broken pieces off, then clean the wound, and pull out the fragments if they are separated; and if they are not separated, then let the wound rot, which will make the extractions easier. And for other wounds in other limbs, judgement should be as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The ruptures of the belly are large, medium, and small; sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out of a large wound, and closing it is more difficult; and often, a small wound is worse than a large one, because the intestines are harder to put back in, if they are not put back in place piece by piece; because the intestines swell immediately when they feel the cold, so they return to their place more easily, and that is why it is better to leave small wounds open, so as to put the intestines back in their place gradually. And know that the ruptures of the belly are according to four manners: the two common sutures happen in the suture of the belly, and the sutures of other wounds of the body and two other proper sutures are common to other wounds; but they are more specific to the suture of the belly, and I will describe each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestines is outside, and it is difficult to put back, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when (the intestines) are cold, warm them in the following way: moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth in warm water only, or cook it in a decoction of wormwood, cypripedium and pepper, and sprinkle the intestines until the swelling is gone; and sometimes use this vinegar remedy, and it is often effective for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling separate, moistEN the intestines with vinegar or bitter and evil-tasting herbs, as this alleviates the opening for a little while; and if it cannot be entered, make an opening in the wound with the instrument used to cut out hemorrhoids; and the first cure is more important than the cutting, that nothing should be cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument to split it: cut inside the curve and not through, and see the shape here:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines come out, put them back in their natural shape and proper place, if you have the power to do so, for this is better than moving them around.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is large, and it is in the lower abdominal area, then you should make the patient lie on their back and place their legs higher than their head. And if it is in the lower part of the belly, then you should put the head and chest higher than the injured parts. And likewise, if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then you should ensure that the injured part is higher than the other. And so, you should manage what I am saying in large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, prepare what is necessary, then take a compress and hold the entire wound with your hand, bringing the edges together. This is the common method of suturing, which consists of taking a needle or more, depending on the size of the wound, leaving two spaces from the edge of the wound, and inserting the needle where there is good, strong thread. And puncture both layers of the skin with both layers of the subcutaneous tissue, which is beneath the skin, as far as you can penetrate it in that part, and bring the two ends of the subcutaneous tissue together in four parts. Then bind a double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring the two edges of the wound together, leaving two spaces, and insert another needle. Then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue doing this as many times as you need to sew up the entire wound. The needles should be medium-sized, between fine and thick, because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot penetrate well. Therefore, they should be of medium size. And it is important not to insert the needles too far from the flesh and skin, because this will open and widen the wound before it heals. Then trim the ends of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while they sleep, and place bandages or cloths at the ends of the needles to keep them in place, leaving them until the wound is healed. And this method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because a second stitch is sufficient for larger ones. The second stitch consists of bringing together the two layers of skin and subcutaneous tissue with one needle or strong medium thread. When you have punctured all four layers together, then turn the needle back to where you began, in the manner of sewing fabric. And leave a space between each stitch the size of a small finger; this type of stitch is known by people. I once sewed up a wound that a man had on his stomach, which was cut with a knife, and the wound was more than a palm's length wide, and two palms deep, and it was in the middle of the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I set the intestines back in place after they had been outside for XXIV hours, and the wound healed within XV days, and I treated it, and it was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I placed clean old cotton on the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and insert it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced straight through, leave the tip of the siphac or thread on the inside where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the inside to the outside; and the technique of this stitch is that you sew just like a pelterer does with furs, leaving the siphac once on one side and taking it up again on the other, until the stitching is fully complete.[Note: A "pelterer" is a person who makes or sells pelts or fur garments. The reference to their technique suggests that the stitches should be evenly spaced and consistently sized.]
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second manner of suturing, which Galen speaks of specifically, is as follows: some people bring two natural parts together and apply one chief part of the suture to the other chief part in such a way. First, insert a needle or chief part of the thread close by, and only pierce that spot, leaving the two edges of the wound; then turn the needle and make it pass from the outside to the inside, through the two edges of the wound; then make both the outside and the inside pass through, in two other holes of the thread that are on the other side; and this is the stronger manner of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galen says this word, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread in it; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather; and know that when the rupture is inside the belly, the suturing is more difficult than at other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh, with all its blood, so that the flesh has moved it, then put back the intestines, and the cut; then put on powder that dries up flesh, and if the flesh has moved it, then put on some ointment that is at hand, until the wound closes; and drain the veins, and let the sutures and the miracles be bound; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to close, old cotton, and move it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 For you do not need any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound may communicate with the principal members, then you should moisten light linen in oil of tempered warmth, or in rose oil, and place it around the edges, and beneath the buttocks; and if he feels pain or putrefaction in the belly, and this happens often, then you should enema him with warm black wine, and similarly if the putrefaction comes as far as the intestines; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is wounded, and this is due to the multitude of veins that are there, and the subtlety of the entire body, and its similarity in nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the ear slips out of the wound, put it back in place as you would with the intestines, while it is still fresh; and if it is old and turned black or blue, tie off the blackened area to prevent bleeding, since there are veins and arteries there; then cut away the tissue between the knot and place the two parts of the ear hanging down from the part below the wound until it heals, to ease the extraction when the ear falls off, and let the wound close.
de la routure dou boueil	of the breaking open of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestines are protruding and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I have seen that a man was stabbed in the abdomen with a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and became inflamed and developed into a fistula, and there was excretion and flatulence coming out; I treated it as best I could and did not stop working on it until it healed and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it soldered, I feared that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he had no pain, but rather improved in condition, eating and drinking; and some experienced ones said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in such a manner: take fat with large knobs, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the fat has opened its mouth, place it between the two edges so that it pulls the edges apart; and then cut off its head, and this holds so that it cannot come undone, then put another fat in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is covered; and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 This joint/hip if it burns in the interior, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the interior with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner: take the head of this intestinal filament, which is very stripped of flesh, and then tie the head of this intestinal filament to a thin twisted linen thread, then insert the thread into the needle and sew the intestine, and pull it together at the opening; and this method of suturing is not outside the path of prudence and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no other means or help, except for delicacy.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or where it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that any wound or abscess, when it matures, is commonly called a "fistula," and similarly when it is deep and wide.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And a fistula is, according to the truth, a hard and white swelling, without pain, as hollow as the feather of a bird; sometimes clear and wide, and other times thick; sometimes shallow, and other times deep; and I have spoken in the classification of wounds, that any wound that has not healed, and there is no flesh, it is not due to anything but one of the Nine causes: namely, due to the small amount of blood or flesh; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips, preventing the growth of flesh; or if it is too wide; or if the place is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or if the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is of the nature of a pestilence; or because the property of the region delays digestion and healing, and swells by nature; or if there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the cures with medicines in the classification.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to let you know the treatment of fistula, which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that a fistula can happen in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the syphilis, or at the intestines, or at the bladder, or at some of the ribs, or at the spine of the back, or at some joint of the hands or feet; and some of them reach the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all fistulas of this kind are of difficult healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I mentioned, and you have trust in the cure, and you recognize it, then take a probe of steel or iron, if the fistula is straight, then seek it; and if the fistula is twisted, then search for it with a delicate probe of lead, for lead bends around the twist; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot search for it with probes, then irrigate it through one of the holes, for moisture easily travels from one hole to another, and cleanse it; then seek it skillfully as much as you can, so that you know if there is bone or nerve in it, and if it is embedded deep, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or any of the places I mentioned to you, then operate on it as I have said, and remove the abscess and corrupt flesh that are inside; and then cure it until it heals, and if the fistula is deeply embedded in the right place, then operate deeply, as much as you can, then put moist bandages with medicine on it, and push them to the end of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then put healing ointments on clean flesh, until it heals; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupt from the fistula, then operate to remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If vein or nerve does not trouble you in the main members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, let the king (cauterize) until all corruption is removed, then cure the injured flesh with appropriate remedies until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns to its previous state, know that you have not yet reached the source: uncover and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is healed in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it; in this case, there is no other means but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone that is corrupt and you can extract it with pincers, do so with a suitable instrument for the task; and if there are many bones, extract all of them, not leaving any behind; and if moisture (pus) opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut away the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something foul-smelling on the wound to promote putrefaction, and leave it until the area around the bones becomes rotten, and then the bones will come apart more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh bone, then simply allow the corruption to set in until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of the corruption, and it reaches the marrow of the bone, then it must be covered and bandaged until the corruption is healed, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 A young man of around thirty years old had pain in his leg due to an internal cause, such that matter came into the leg and caused a large abscess, and there was no obvious reason to open it; but the physicians, in their foolishness, operated on the abscess so much that it opened and a lot of matter drained out, and it became a fistula, and a great deal of pus came out, all of which smelled foul; and for two years many physicians treated him, and there was no skillful physician in the art of healing until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines they were using to treat him, and the matter that was draining out of the wounds; and the young man's skin became red, and he had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I set up a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one came toward the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I hurried then, and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the rot reached to the bone inside; I thought what appeared of the rotten bone was all that there was, except for what I removed; and I began to restore the wound with soaking medicines for a long time, and it could not heal; and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the rot continuing in the bone, and I thought it was the same, and then I removed it, and took care to heal the wound; but I could not do so until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and broke it all the way through, then I restored it with medicines; and it healed and joined quickly, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For through the evacuation of blood, he often sweated, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone, hard flesh grew, and it was of good disposition and caused no harm or contrary effect at all, neither when walking nor standing.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this way: take a bandage and pull on the end of the bone that is visible, and command someone to hold it up; and place another larger linen bandage over the skin that is above the bone, and stretch it so as to draw the rotten flesh underneath, and uncover the flesh above the place where you want to be cauterized, so that the hot iron or a board does not burn the healthy flesh; and it is necessary to cauterize until one can see and feel that the corruption has been removed, and cauterize again if needed.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is rotten and not visible, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, reveal all the flesh; then put a piece of ember underneath, and then apply silk from one side to the other side of the corruption, and let the silk be one finger's width away from the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut the rotten joint and cover the bone or what it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other option but to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or in the ankle of the foot, this is a very difficult thing, but nonetheless you must examine the corruption, how it appears to you; and clean it in every way that you can, except let the vein or nerve not prevent you; and know that there are many incisors and silks for cutting these bones, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their length and shortness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each type of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the evidence of the types of diseases; so consider the instrument you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The hips rot away either from within or from without; and when you have treated this corruption with the cure of medicines, and it does not help, then one must cover the member down to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes from death, or from the greater evil, which is the defect of the member; and the sign is that the member becomes black, so that it seems it has been burnt by fire, and after the blackness, the corruption goes from member to member, and takes hold throughout the body; so one must hurry to cover it, and if it is due to the sting of any venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and the like, if the corruption is in the joint of the finger, then one should cover it, and not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches the hand, take hold of the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut with a knife; and if it surpasses the knife, it is deadly, and there is no remedy but the amount of its power; and do thus whenever the corruption comes to a point: if it comes to the first joint, then take hold after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, then cut all of the foot; and if it rises in the leg, then cut at the joint of the knee; and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other means but to let the patient die; and the manner of cutting or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below, and stretch out a suture on either side of the incision, and you sever the flesh that is between the two sutures to the width of one span, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or sew, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the suture does not touch the healthy place, and come to the patient another lesion and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if bleeding occurs while you are working, then cauterize the area quickly, or apply tightening powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you of an incident that happened to a man in my presence: he had a blackening that looked like burns from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his foot toe, so that it spread throughout his foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover his foot, and was healed; and long after, the corrosion returned to his hand toe, and he came to me, and I applied reactive substances after the cleansing of the body, but the corrosions could not be stopped; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, for I had hope of reversing the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for his vitality was weak; and he despaired completely and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have only told this story so that one may act accordingly, if in need.
