And when one wants to be bled, in any manner, it is necessary that they cleanse the intestines with a light enema if they have retained a lot of feces, so that the veins do not draw out impurities from the intestines that could harm the main members; and one should not bleed someone who is overly full of food, nor those who are intoxicated until they are sober, nor those who are edematous; and if one wishes to be bled after a colic attack, vomiting, stomach upset, frequent urination from women, work, staying up late, fasting, or any other exhaustion of the body or injury to the body; then refine the humors if the blood is thick by means of food and drink and medicines if you have the means; then enter the bath if nothing prevents it, to further refine the blood, and bleed from the vein in the lower arm near the elbow, as we have said; and rest that day from work, exertion, lust, and similar things; and be joyful and happy, and let the one doing the bleeding raise their sleeve higher than the arm of the person being bled, and rub the upper arm two or three times, then loosen the ligature in the middle, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow; and then rub the area around the vein with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the bandage with a little oil, then place your left hand on the vein below the area to be bled, so that the vein does not move and is not missed when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 Because there are veins that run like strings in the skin, and some of them are full of airiness, such that when one applies fire, they contract and cannot be opened; it is thus necessary for the surgeons to be aware of these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, then try again a little below or quickly above that level, unless the place is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the wound is swollen and the patient is frightened, let it be for a day or two and do not bind the arm; perhaps abscesses will come; do not enter into the bath, then resume the bleeding if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, or the blood coagulates subtly and you doubt that it will not bleed enough, then apply the flame directly into that opening; and perform the procedure somewhat quickly, so that the swelling does not increase; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the place swollen, do not restart the bleeding, but put a little bit of oil residue on it, for it lightens the body from blood, and the oil becomes thicker in this place; and thus administer the oil residue in every bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and do the same with triacle and wound dressing, when they are put on the place; spreading the blood subtly if it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, even when it is only bled once at the time when the vein's opening is small, then hurry and put on the place a wet sponge with warm water and salt; and hold it there for an hour. It is necessary to do this after the blood flow from the vein has stopped. And if there remains some black or green color on the place for several days, it does not harm; and if you see it, put something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in rue juice on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there comes an abscess and appearance of discharge at the basis of the big toe; place then your hand on it, and if you find a soft spot upon compression of the hand, it is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be cautious not to apply any of the things we have mentioned, as it may accidentally cut an artery; instead make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each person according to the quantity of their vitality and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if it appears thick, let it continue to flow until it thins out; and if it is too warm, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for one who is stout and robust, and in need of bloodletting, to make a larger incision, and let the wound be wide; and for the weak, do the contrary, and it is necessary to bleed him little and often, and it should be bled by cutting across, not by puncturing; and this method of bleeding is safe from loss of blood and injury to nerves, and is worth more than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 And for one whose body needs bleeding, it is necessary to give them bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if they are feverish, let blood three or four times; and if they have a cold complexion, feed them before the bleeding with bread soaked in muscat syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and anise, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he has a fracture, after the exit of much blood, then it is necessary that he drink broth of meat, and fragrant subtle syrup, and make use of other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed from the arm and purge himself again, then it is necessary, when he has become weak due to great loss of blood, that he bleeds a little at a time, in accordance with the amount of his remaining strength, continuously.[*check the spelling of "afoiblis"]
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And he who wishes to bleed from the arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong body, should bleed again 7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wants to heal from another part, they should heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood inside the body which is already heated and causes fever; so it is necessary to draw out a large quantity and widen the opening until it clots with pus; then you should pay attention to all the conditions of fracture, and place your hand on the pulse when it is fracturing, so that death does not come instead of pus, and this happens many times when the one treating the fracture is negligent; and it is not at all necessary, when you unbind the arm and make blood exit a second time, and the opening is closed, for you to press hard; nor if it is curved, for him to extend his arm quickly, for that would be harmful; but let it be until it fractures a second time; or you apply the tip of the flame, so that the clotted blood at the opening of the vein comes out, and place a piece of wet cloth on top, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then leave it alone and do not squeeze it at all, until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a need to draw blood again, then heal it in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healed at the location of the chief vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of bleeding is as follows: let the patient put his hand in warm water until the vein becomes red; then bind it moderately so that the vein shows clearly; then bleed him crosswise, not lengthwise or widthwise; and make the incision large, and let it be bled close to the joint of the hand, and if no blood comes out, put the hand back in warm water and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for it is more necessary to do so in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than any other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The sap of the salvation plant of the right hand is worthwhile for all liver ailments, and this is how: strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein swells, if one sees it; and if the sap flows sideways, and if you scrape it all off completely, it does no harm; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are underneath entirely stripped of flesh, and then return the hand to hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn enough blood as is necessary, then put oil and wax on the vein to quickly seal it up, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The letting of blood from the left hand is good for disease of the spleen, and do the same as I have told you regarding the right side (hand).
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The sap of the sophera is worthwhile for all ailments that are below the body, such as diseases of the womb, retention of menstrual flow, and illnesses of the kidneys, thighs, and old legs, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the qualities of his bleeding are such that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it disappears, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and a great deal of blood comes out above the foot; therefore, bleed where the flow is greater, either at the ankle or above it, whichever is more convenient.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed on the foot, be cautious of the nerves that are beneath and also bleed across (the vein) as when cutting; and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the water and allow the vein to empty completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if the bleeding is insufficient the first time, try again a little higher up, for the place is salty; and do not worry about cutting a nerve, as we have said; and do the same for the shin of the other leg as well.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the back of the heel, and its bleeding is worth as much as the pain of a swelling, when it is due to hot blood.[Important note: This translation is provided for educational purposes only, and should not be used as medical advice. Always consult with a healthcare professional for medical issues.]
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the qualities of his bleeding are such that the patient enters into a bath and squeezes above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, bleed in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and it is better to make many incisions, for the place is dry, and the vein is deeply embedded in most men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't find it there, seek out a vein on the outside of the leg, near the small toe, and beware of nerves; and let enough blood flow until you see fit, then loosen the tie and apply cotton and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 cup-shaped suction cups (lit. "sained" or "purged suction cups)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: by striking to draw blood or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this cupping therapy, which is done without striking, is of two kinds: one is with heat, and the other is without heat. The cupping therapy that is done by striking and drawing blood is performed in fourteen parts of the body, one of which is at the very top of the head; another is at the neck; two are on each side of the collarbone; one is under the chin; two are on each shoulder; two are on the hips; two are on each arm; two are on each leg; and two are on each ankle. The cupping therapy does not draw large amounts of blood, but rather only small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken a person as much as venesection does. Furthermore, cupping therapy should not be administered in any disease caused by excess until the entire body has been evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to perform bloodletting, or for customary purposes, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at all times; for there are some who, when they need bloodletting, have a heavy head; and there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are such ones who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and secrete blood; and there are some who dream, and see through night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and also when it is mid-month, we order them to be bled after 3 hours of daylight.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The letting of blood from the nose helps with head cracks that come to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body; and this bloodletting is in place of the letting of blood from the head, and it is not suitable for those of a cold complexion to use, or who have catarrh, because it harms them greatly; and for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who frequently use it become forgetful, and therefore one should place the cup a little lower out of caution for forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventilation to the neck is located near the bloodletting of the head and the basilic vein, and this is why it is useful for constriction of the breast and splitting of the channel of the throat, and for all [kinds of] suffocation; and it should be gently applied, for if it stays in place too firmly, it can cause oblivion or stomach/heart problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventilation to the two ribs of the neck is useful for headaches, eyestrain, migraines, strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is located near the bloodletting of the basilic vein; and you should instruct the surgeon to place his hand gently, so as not to cut the artery and cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Wind relieving beneath the chin is beneficial for diseases of the mouth, and inflammation of the gums, and similar illnesses in the mouth; and it is a substitute for bloodletting at the two lips.[STHAPHANUS:] It seems that the author is describing here a form of cupping therapy (a method of treatment using heated cups placed on the skin to create suction) as an alternative to phlebotomy, or bloodletting, in order to treat various medical conditions. The text suggests that this technique can be used at different locations on the body, such as the neck and the area beneath the chin, to address a range of health issues. It is important to note that while cupping therapy can have some therapeutic benefits, it should only be performed by a trained and qualified medical professional in order to minimize the risk of injury or infection.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Wind relieving at the shoulders is beneficial for illness caused by heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 Wounds of the thigh are as significant as those of three arms' veins, for they draw blood from these large veins; and it instructs the physician not to strike too deep, for the place is bare of flesh and has nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is on the rump is as valuable for hemorrhoids of the anus and diseases beneath (the anus), and the cupping glass should be large and made of iron, because it needs to pull well; and perhaps, if it were too fine, it would break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs heal openly because they draw blood from the whole body and are valuable for old pains in the loins, hips, bladder, and they bring out boils; and they are located over the two shins and ankles, yet even so they weaken the body after long use, and cause paralysis in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cup is as follows: place it empty first and apply it gradually, and do so quickly, and shake it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see that the place becomes red and swollen, and the darkening of the blood appears; then pierce it, and replace the cups, and pay attention to the condition of the body, for there are those who have thin skin and clear pores: it is necessary to pierce only once, and it is necessary to make large and rather deep wounds; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, then you must pierce it twice: the first time to thin the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, then you must pierce it a third time; and when we want to draw little by little, once is enough for us.[Repeated text removed.]
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want much blood, let us apply the cups frequently; and if the blood is thick, strike deep; and the goal is to quickly pierce the heart, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cups with warming and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of cucurbit seeds; and if it is in winter, with oil of watercress, lilies, chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluidities are abundant and cold, take wormwood oil, or balm mint oil, or anise oil, and similar.[ST1]
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one who is being treated has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied, but it should be washed with water after ventosation (the act of exposing a body part to fresh air) of rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or any similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have too much moisture, should get up from easels, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those who have large superfluities (excess fluids) should get up from old wine, or the water of the sick, or the decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and one should not be bled with cupping glasses before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and one should not sleep after the ventosation (exposing to fresh air), and it is necessary that they wash themselves, both when they are about to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And be aware if the one who is healing is of a choleric nature, and if his blood is too thick and inflamed; then they should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at ease, and similar things; and eat easily digestible foods, and meat of chicken, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And for those of a cold complexion, they should take syrup of honey and half-aged wine, which is between old and new, and eat soft foods, and eat easily digestible foods and small birds and pigeons; and on the day that they will be bled, they should drink more than they eat; and it is appropriate to give some people a triacle or muscatel before or after the bleeding, to comfort the main members; and let the blood be thinned, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 Cups that are placed without striking are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach and groin and legs, for these members do not tolerate being struck, and one does not place them there except to draw blood from member to member, as we place them on the breasts when milk is flowing; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cups on the stomach and on the groin to reduce the member; and to alleviate pain when there is an obstruction or stone, as it can possibly draw out the obstruction with its attractive virtue, or dislodge the stone from its place; and it does this when placed on the liver and spleen when there is trapped wind, and these cups are administered empty in order to suction only; and sometimes they are administered assembled with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the cup with hot water, or with water in which helpful herbs for this purpose have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping cup applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and have on the side near the middle a small hole, as big as to put a needle through, and be made of brass, smooth before so that it does not prick the patient when putting it on the member; and have in the middle a rod of brass or iron, to hold a candle in place, and let there be both large and small [blisters/suction cups], according to the illnesses and age of those who use them; for the blisters/suction cups of children are different than those of the elderly, and of the thin compared to those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And one should place this blister/suction cup on the member in this way: light a candle of wax or linen, and put it crosswise through the rod that is inside the blister/suction cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the blister/suction cup, but not close enough to burn the patient; then place it on the member, with your fingers covering the hole we mentioned earlier, so that when you want to release the air, you remove the blister/suction cup; and relight the candle as before, and repeat this process as needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the cup which is applied in case of pleurisy, it has no rod or opening, and is not applied except when it is full of water, and is placed only on the member; and this is the method:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Blisters are not applied except to parts where cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and to bare areas of flesh, such as the fingers or nose, and other similar places. And the quality of the water should be such that when you find blisters in clear, sweet water without putrefaction, you take them; and place them in clean, fresh water until they become familiar (accustomed), and have nothing left in their bellies; and then let it be purged with leeches and cups, then rub the member until it becomes red, and place the blisters on it; and when they are full, and begin to itch, if it is a place where a cup can be placed, place one there, for it is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, lift the leg of the hip, and then of the thigh, very well, and then stretch it; and if the leg remains swollen for too long after the body of the veins, wet a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling is multiplied, put crushed vitriol, or alum, and similar things, on it until it subsides; or you put half of peeled beans on the area, and leave them until they dry at the spot, which will stop the bleeding immediately; and if you need more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the veins do not want to clot, rub the spot with fresh blood, or stick a needle in it until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will coagulate; and when you see that they stop, sprinkle a little bit of aloe and crushed salt, or ash, on it, and they will immediately clot.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and deals with the setting of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know, dear son, that foolish surgeons throw away this chapter, as they never saw any of the ancient books, nor did they read letters; and for this reason, the knowledge is strange in our land, for I never found any good one; and I know nothing, except for the knowledge from the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have extracted the knowledge, and through experience, and through the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, as I did in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we now speak of the prologue of this book, where we will summarize the contents and chapters in which the sage puts his understanding and dwells on the truth, so that those who are proven (experienced) may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or breakage comes to anyone, you must hurry to heal the patient from one side and the other, if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of the body, children, the elderly; or if the weather is not extremely hot or too cold; and eat only lean food, that is to say, cold meats, and bird and hare meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you are certain that there will be no hot abscess or spreading of matter to the limb; so let the patient return to their usual regimen.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that promote thick nutrition, such as wheat boiled in water, and rice, and testicles, and cow's udder, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the swelling will subside and the fracture will heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot heal or join together well according to their nature due to the weakness of their limbs, nor can those who are too young, such as the bones of small children. But it doesn't matter, reset the broken bone and use large, sturdy bandages that hold and bring the limb together, until it heals as it was before; and do not disturb its work, and for this reason, you must feed them hearty meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different than the break of the hip or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes along the line (of the bone), and another at an angle, like the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a break with a wound, and a break with a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And for each type there is its own tool and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory brings to mind; and the break of the bone is known by the limb being twisted, and it is apparent from the outside, and sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break; but there can be twisting, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not appropriate to move it with your hand, but place medicine that comes after this, and then gently bind it.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that fractures that are in a tree, and are the two parts disjointed, they must now be aligned equally, so that abscesses do not come there; and if abscesses do come there, let him leave it for some days, until the abscess is calmed down; then align it evenly as you can easily and neatly, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration of one where pieces are missing; then bind it, as will be necessary hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if in the bone there are broken pieces, stretch it from two sides, whether it is an arm or a leg, or with your hand if it is a small member, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; and place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, align all the connections in their places as you can; and make sure that through your work, no harm or pain comes to the patient; and join the two ends of the bones well according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand to see if it seems that it is not well aligned: then straighten it nicely and do not pull too hard or press as those who cause hot abscess and constriction in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is healed, chastise the patient well so that they do not move it, whether awake or sleeping, turning or in any other way; and make sure that the limb is secured so that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when they feel any pain, it is not yet healed, and it must be put in such a position that they feel no pain; and make sure that it is set straight, so that there are no deformities when it is healed; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and largeness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and the like: they should be wrapped in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as hips and legs: they should be wrapped in a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the entire large limb and constrain it equally from all sides, so that there is no swelling; then wrap light cotton around it three or four times according to the limb, and pull your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go above the break and pull less, so that the break moves slightly away; and loosen the bandage a little at a time until you encompass a large part of the healthy limb, then take another bandage and wrap around again above the broken limb; then return to the part below the break, and constrain it moderately, not too tight or too loose, as we have said in the first place; then place linen or cloth wadding between the bandages, so that it is even on all sides, then tie everything with a bandage on top, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is swelling or abscess, place something warm and soothing for abscesses on it, and that removes the swelling, and leave it like that for several days; then apply pressure with your fingertips, using a bandage one half as wide as a reed, or a piece of wood used to make roof shingles, or palm fronds, and arrange it in this manner:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 but it is necessary that the splint put on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others; and also be as long as is appropriate for the size or smallness of the limb; then apply pressure with your fingertips as you did at the first location, then bind a suitable thread over it, just as you did at the first location on the fracture; tighter is better, less so; and the thread should be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen done by foolish people who bind their injuries with twine, this is a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two fingers' width of space between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the grooves after tightening on healthy parts, place under them linen or wool padding, so that they do not wound themselves.[Comment: This section suggests a method of treating wounds caused by overtight binding.]
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture and the flesh is torn, I will tell you the treatment as follows. (Translation note: "li keurs" means the meat or flesh.)[Comment: This section signals a transition to a new topic in the medical text, which appears to be about treating wounds associated with bone fractures.]
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to constrict all broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the member is large, one should not apply splints until after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on the certainty of a hot abscess arising; and here is the method of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: it is that you take flour that holds on to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this concoction, not too clear nor too thick, and use it; and this is the common method of the restorative poultice for many types of fractures, and similarly for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of poultice to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: take three drams each of barley, ladanum, endive, asafoetida, gum arabic, and mallow; five drams each of myrrh and aloes; nine drams of alechil; and grind them into a powder, then mix with egg yolk. If the patient's complexion is hot, use this poultice, as it has a good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and benefits many men.[Reference(s):
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another method of poultice for twisting: take violet and mallow, 10 parts each; myrrh and aloe, 9 parts each; acacia 6 parts; and Armenian bole, 10 parts, and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another way of plaster for joints and separated bones in their places, and to appease the resulting pain, and for the cure of bone wounds and fractures: take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not restore [the bone] but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly removes pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of emplaster that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and crushed leaves of the terrestrial pea plant, grind them together, and make an emplaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way of plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to lessen the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, fine wheat flour, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is hot, mix it with moist coriander water or just water, and use it.[NOTE: I assume "vismalve" means "mallow", as there is no such word in French]
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another manner of emplaster, stronger than the first, when hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take root of mallow, seeds of flax, valerian, melilot, and sanicle, and flowers of violets and camomile, all in equal parts; and grind, and make into a paste with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not place anything on the broken limb to restore it, except for a cautery made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be moderate, not too hard or too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen thinks one should place on the broken limb, to restore it, dry and slightly warm things, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another type of ointment that is good for wounds and pain: take a dog's liver and chopped off men's hair or bird feathers, and also chamomile, and similarly, grind them up, and make an ointment with it and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then loosen it a little afterward, and take care if the patient does not feel any pain, nor have the bones moved from their place; if so, do not loosen it for many days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth and sea sponge, and dip in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it to a cushion, until you are sure of fever; and relieve the inflammation of the member, and remove the pain, then gently bandage again, and a little plaster, and do not tighten it as much as before; and delicately, until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is heated and red and painful and swollen has been removed completely, and you need poultice and bandage, then begin again as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no improvement comes to the member from what we have mentioned, do not unlock it until after three days, or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, so that the breaker can wait and bring the adjustment of the flesh closer; then hold it tighter than before, and the flesh will swell, as I said before; and if you see the place drying out more than necessary, know that no numbness can come there; therefore, anoint it with warm water each time you unlock it, every third day, and slightly loosen the ligature; thus, the numbness to the member is cut off, and it quickly heals what foolish doctors do, who incorrectly restore the crooked member: this is bad, and such work is frightening, and I see no other option but to leave it and work on it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the different ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many kinds of fractures exist, with various shapes, and different causes; for there are fractures that are made by the striking of a sword, and the neck takes out all the bone down to the syphax which is beneath the bone, as done by a hatchet or stick; and this kind of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or when the sword chops the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called an "absolue" (complete) fracture; and the wound caused by these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded blow, or a split (fracture), or a stone chip, or from falling on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a fracture that reaches up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that lodges in the bone as thin as a hair, and the break is small, and for this reason it is called "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or by some similar thing, and forces a piece of bone inward, and the location is hidden, just like when blacksmiths hammer on cauldrons; then it enters inside the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, such as children's heads; and it happens in all these types of fractures where small pieces are separated, like so; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the drawing away from them, and the investigation by tents, and by the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is recognized by those who, when they have uncovered the bone and rubbed it, make the fracture appear black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be careful about the patient's symptoms, and if you see any adverse effects, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, feverish chills, eyes bulging out and reddening, and other similar signs in various dispositions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any terrifying symptoms, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it's in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest when you are able to.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue underneath the bone does not become corrupt and the complications that we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the break of the bone comes as far as the membrane covering the brain, then you should split the injured part in this way: that is, you take hold of the patient's wounded head and expose the bone in all the ways you can, and gently along the wound's shape, and if blood flow or abscess comes from exposing the bone, you help it with what is needed, and it is that you fill the hole with cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess subsides, and make sure there is no more blood flow; then begin to remove the bone, and this is done in two ways: one way is to cut in a narrow incision in front, and that is the method:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put in another incision, larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have several different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and protruding, you must pierce around it, so that you make incisions with terets (a cylindrical tool), not too deep that they go beyond the bone of the skull, and above the tip there should be a margin or circle, so that the tip does not go beyond the bone; and you need to have several of them, so that each one comes in its place along the width of the bone, so that you have terets for all bones; and this is the form of the three types of terets.[Speaker]: I see, so the text is describing a medical procedure for treating an injury involving bone protrusion. The practitioner is advised to make incisions around the bone, using tools called "terets", with a margin or circle above the tip of each one to ensure that they do not go beyond the bone. The text also notes that multiple terets should be used, so that they cover the entire width of the bone. It seems like this is the continuation from the previous translation about fire cautery and other medical procedures, with a focus on treating injuries involving bones.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The way to pierce around the broken bone is to place a teret on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then move the teret to another place after a little while, and do the same all around, then cut the space of the bone between the holes with incisors (a tool for cutting), making it as delicate and light as possible, so that you draw out the bone with your hand or with any of the tools you have such as tongs, pliers; and make sure that you do not touch the brain or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced and treated the bone, you should restore the sharpness that remains of the bone to all other instruments similar to a scalpel, but it should be more slender and fine than the other scalpels; and if any small bones or splinters remain, gently remove them with the instruments; then cure the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is as described by Galen, which is safer, and he praised it highly, and this is his word:[From here, I'm assuming you want me to translate what follows in the text, attributed to Galen]
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover part of the bone where the break appears clear; so that when you have exposed it, place the round head of this lancet-shaped instrument beneath it, as shown in the diagram.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut from one side, and leave the part jagged on two edges, so that the cut is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet so that you lightly chop the bone all around, and take great care of the cloth that is underneath; if it is adhered to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate down to the cloth, and the bone is only cut through at the top, and there are small pieces; then you must smooth out that roughness, and remove the splinters with a sharp razor, which you should have in various sizes, to adjust according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	First use large razors, then fine ones, and do not stop doing so until it is smooth.[Still working on this project! I will let you know if I have any questions or need further assistance.]
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other subtle hair cuttings and fractures, it is necessary to arrange things according to their alignment; and this is not an easy task even for one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 And if the abscess is uncovered, take a linen cloth of appropriate size for the wound, soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled cloth, soaked in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; do this as lightly as you can, without harming the abscess. Then apply another ligament over it, but not so tight as to only cover the wound; leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscess has calmed down. Afterward, untie it and apply medicine such as lily roots, vetches flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, reapplying the medicine without biting; ensure that the wound remains clean, free of any pus accumulation.
