Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is intact and complete, you must quickly reset it and not delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and places his folded hand into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and let the other hand be free to align equally; and command the patient to relax and move his jaw from side to side.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician adjusts it evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the returning is difficult, even if it involves both jaws together, soak them with warm water and oil, until you can easily adjust them; do not delay in making the adjustment, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are aligned evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without difficulty, then place wet bandages soaked in a mixture of rose oil and wax on it, then bind it lightly with soft bindings; and let the patient sleep on their back, with his head between two pillows, so that he does not move it to the right or left, nor strive to chew, but eat light food until the pain is gone, and the jaw has healed; and then eat what you want lightly, and do not strain to open your mouth to eat or drink, until the jaw is well healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be restored to their place in an hour and are not returned to their proper position, then fevers and chronic coughs may develop, and perhaps gastrointestinal disturbances, and possibly vomiting of bile.[*]
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a dire situation; and many who experience it die within nine days.[*]
de la forcelle	of the fork/fracture/dislocation
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation cannot be dislodged from the side and the chest, and is sometimes dislodged outward, which can be felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is as follows: let the patient lie flat on their back and extend their arms; then press firmly with your palm on the joint, and it will return; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it; and the hip that is dislocated towards the leg cannot come out; if not, and if it dislocates at any time, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and similarly, the hip joint is put back in place when it is dislocated from its position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder does not dislocate except in three ways: one of which is when it dislocates at the part of the socket beneath; and the second way is at the part of the blade; and perhaps it dislocates at the upper part, but this happens rarely; and it never dislocates backwards towards the shoulder blade, nor does it dislocate inwards towards the nerves; and more often than not, it dislocates downward towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, for it slips out quickly in them; in those who have enough flesh, it slips out with difficulty and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men that they suffer a blow or fracture, and their shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should examine it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that the dislocation is when it goes down towards the shoulder blade, and there is a difference between the sick and the healthy shoulder, and you will find a clear distinction between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit, and below the shoulder blade where you touch the top of the shoulder, just like an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck, nor make any movements; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly when you touch; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to set back in place, when it is new, or when the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is as follows: the caregiver raises the patient's hand high, then places their cheeks beneath the shoulder blade and forcefully lifts the joint upward to its place. The caregiver then raises the arm and extends it high, before placing it back down, causing it to quickly return to its proper position.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come back as we have said before, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and a soothing and relaxing ointment should be applied, such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and it should be applied; then the patient should be propped up on his back, and a soft wool cushion should be placed under the shoulder blade, neither too hard nor too soft; then have the healer place his talus (ankle bone) on the cushion, and lift the top of the shoulder forcefully, and pull the hand of the patient; and another assistant should hold the head of the patient so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will come back immediately if you see it being reset in this manner: and it is necessary to have a person present who is stronger than the patient; and stand at his side, and push his shoulder under the patient's shoulder blade, and lift the shoulder blade upwards, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another assistant should pull the hand of the patient down towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, have them hold something heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And the dislocation can also be reset in another way: by inserting a long stake into the ground, so that the patient's head rests on it like a pillow, and neither too thick nor too thin; then place the patient beneath it, with soft cloths under them, and have the patient lie down on the long stake; then stretch out their other hand far away, and the joint will quickly return to its place; and if it still does not want to return despite all that we have said, perform this treatment: take a stake of two arms in length and four digits wide, with a pointed tip to enter deep beneath the armpit, in this manner.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place soft cloths on top of the stake so that the stake does not wound the patient, then place it beneath the patient's armpit. Extend his arm along the length of the stake and tie the shoulder to the stake as well, with the hand placed at the end of the stake. Then lift the entire arm up onto a step of a ladder or some sort of stool, so that the hand hangs freely downwards. In this way, the joint will return to its place now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is dislocated, whatever the cause may be, you should place a wool sphere of even height under the shoulder blade, then put a poultice corresponding in size made of powder from the mill, with incense and egg yolk, all over the shoulder and around, then bind it tightly under the shoulder blade, and turn the bandage over the poultice, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he should eat only soft food until the limb is strengthened, as it will heal faster; and then eat normally after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, then you should apply cauteries to it at three points, as is set out in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it becomes dislocated again after 7 days, and the joint does not hold and the patient cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder have been cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is toward the hip, and the breasts, or the back, is made by impact and extension of hands, and another location is administered; and heal until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes cracking in the limb, and slowness in movement, then let the patient take many baths until that cracking is eased, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the ribcage
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the ribcage is dislocated by points, and returns by points; and it is dislocated all around, even in front and back, and the dislocation is not put back in place, for one can see it and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure. (Note: I assume "figure" here means position or aspect)
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick person with the knife to the wound, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must set it (the joint) so that abscesses will come to a head, because if abscesses come to a head, it would be difficult to set; and perhaps it cannot be completely set, especially when it is in the back; this is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the reduction is, when it is of such a state that it can be set, that you hold out his hand with your two hands; and let his arms be stretched out, and let the hands of the practitioner be along the cut, above and below, and bring the joint to its ends, or to the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he bends his hand to his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm the cut that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong traction; and have two people extend the arm, and hold it with two people, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it; and when the physician has aligned the joint with his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns; and when it is in place, apply dry ointment with egg yolk, and hold it firmly, and bend the arm at the patient's neck, and leave it like that for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, he loosens the bandage and leaves it; and if you see that the joint is not well aligned, then reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it for several days until it is securely set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels great pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is eased; or put sheep fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then replace the fat, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times, until it is healed; and if you wish, put moist cow dung warmed with butter, and bind it on; it will return to its place.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return (to its original position) is easy, more so than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be quickly returned to its place in the same hour that it has become dislocated, so that the area becomes swollen or a hot abscess forms there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the resetting is as follows: place the afflicted hand on a table, extend the assistant's hand, and the physician aligns it so that he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns to its place; but it is necessary that you look if it is in the correct position; then have the patient place the back of his hand on a table for the extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and let the physician put his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it now returns (to its proper place), that is good. If not, apply soothing plasters for abscesses and bind it in this manner without moving it.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot bear it and you cannot set it in place after several days, then let the joint remain dislocated; and it will not harm the patient as long as his hand remains moist and he cannot exert any force at all: know that the nerves or arteries are cut; there is no other remedy but to cauterize near the wound, and perhaps this will do some good.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then loosen it and leave it like that.[STOPPING HERE PER YOUR REQUEST.]
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some cracking, moisten it with warm water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the thumbs of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand dislocate on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly; then straighten the finger and push the dislocation towards the knuckles until it returns, then hold the finger's head and bend it towards the side where it is disjointed; and leave it for 2 days, and then make it even on that day; and do not bind it, as we have said, and unbind it during the day, and make it move, and rebind it at night; and do this frequently, until it becomes tight, and similarly do so if it is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and act as you did before, until it is healed; and similarly do so when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the small of the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the small of the back or the neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for the injury quickly kills the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that stools leave involuntarily, and they cannot hold it back, and often certain limbs become weakened, or both thighs or both arms or one, and often the hips move in four ways; the one that moves at the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is to check if "gilbositez" has come from infancy: if it has, there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And the one that comes from falling or impact or similar things, ancient methods of cures say with great solemnity that it is not beneficial in all cases; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention and created various instruments for it.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the swelling that comes to the front of the breast, there is no engine or health; and also that which comes directly in two sides, and cannot be cured unless it is specifically the one that comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient is stretched out on his face evenly, and has support beneath, so that he does not injure himself; then stick one stake firmly in the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a rope underneath the patient's ankles, and another around the calves, and knees, and ankles; and two assistants know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and they are tightly fastened, the stakes as we have said, and the assistant places his palms on the spine very firmly, until it comes back to life.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return to its place with this treatment, take a board of three arms' length, supported at the bottom, and have the patient lie on his side, and place the head of the board under the opening (of the dislocation), then put the middle of the board on the spine; and have the physician place his feet on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see it necessary, do it with a device that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And it is that you drive two stakes into the patient's head, one of arm's length and the other towards the feet, and have between each stake a hand-span of space; and have in each stake one hole, where the device turns, and have them firmly fixed in the ground so they do not move; and between each pair of stakes have one turning stake, on which the ropes turn, and have two small stakes of a hand'spans length for turning the device; and then tie the rope that is between the saddle to the device towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet at the other device, and each assistant turns his device with all the rope, and the master aligns the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is aligned, place a dessicative plaster with an abundance of egg yolk on it, then the wadding, then an elongated stylet of a tablet three fingers long, which reaches the area of the gelatinous tissue and the healthy part of the shoulder blade, then bind it with a ligament as we have said, and have the patient use gentle exercise until it is healed; and if anything comes at the end of the healing process, one should administer softening and soothing medicines, along with the stylet mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered, and sometimes there appears to be a dislocation in the back scapula of the spine, but it is only the bone, so one must not make assumptions: perhaps this could lead to death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that at the joints of the groin and the shoulder, only dislocations occur, not like with other joints; and the joint of the groin is dislocated in four ways: inside and outside, and front and back; and more so on the inside, and less so on the front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears higher than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee by the fire; and the area next to it is swollen due to an abscess, because the hip comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign that it is coming on the outside is that these symptoms are opposite to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of this that occurs to him in front, is that he stretches his leg according to the completion; nevertheless, he does not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot advance, and he holds his urine, and his ankle swells, and when he walks, he steps on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of this that occurs to him in the back, is that he cannot stretch out his knee or bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is relaxed, and the head of the femur is at the side under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The reduction of this similar type of dislocation is that you should look to see if the dislocation is old, and if it remains in its position, then there is no cure for it; and one should not be too eager to act
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for this type of dislocation that is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocations, you should act quickly to return the joint, stretch it inwardly and outwardly, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return to its place and not require any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, you should prepare and strongly hold the leg with two hands, or with a belt tied above the knee; and another assistant extends their hand above in such a way that they push their hands under the patient's arches, then gently bind a soft ligament to the thigh; and another holds the end of the belt; and they all pull up and down at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching is common in four cases, and if the dislocation has returned as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 Or if not, when the dislocation is on the outside, you should turn the patient towards their healthy side, then place the belt on the root of the thigh and the groin area below the inguinal ligament, then pull the belt upwards towards the inguinal ligament and the groin crease; then another assistant takes hold of the patient's arms and strongly embraces the affected thigh, pulling it outward; and the dislocation will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot squeeze it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the patient's two feet together with a strong soft ligature at the heels and at the knees, and let the sick leg be extended two digits more than the other; then let it be hung from the head of a beam, and be above ground two arms' length; then command a minister to embrace the hip's head, and let there be another minister hanging with the patient, who tightly embraces the thigh, for the joints return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is outside, let the patient lie down as we have said in the one with gout, and tighten the ligature on the sick leg properly, and also on the belly; then place two splints, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert one splint between the patient's thighs in the shape; and have a cloth dampened placed around it so that it does not hurt the patient, then each minister stretches out towards him, and let the surgeon put evenly his hand on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place it on (top of) a board and press it as we have said in gilbosité, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, one must quickly stretch out the affected leg as I have said, and the doctor should make an effort to be over the affected ankle, then press with his other hand and pull down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is to the outside, one should not stretch the patient downwards, nor lift them up from the ground. Instead, they should be positioned as if an abscess were on the outside, as we have said in the section on lying on two abscesses; and they should lie on their back, with limbs extended as we have said before. One must then press down on the joint against the table, until the patient stretches out their legs equally. Then adjust the hips, apply a poultice, and bind it with a bandage so that the abscess does not move. Let them rest for three or four days, then loosen the bandage and reapply the poultice. If you see that the legs are equal, bind it again as before, and let them rest for three more days. Then loosen the bandage and have them walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inside and outside, and back; and it never dislocates in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if it does not reach his hip, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such [dislocations] is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his belly, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee with your palms, and pull between your hands, then strongly bend the two sides of the knee; and another minister extends his foot, so that the knee comes back to its place, and the sign is that he easily bends his leg at his hip; and apply the poultice, and make the leg adhere to the hip, and bind them tightly together for three or four days, then loosen [the binding]; and the patient should not exert himself to go, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not in alignment, stretch it strongly, as we have said in the treatment of inflammation, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes dislocated and sometimes completely dislocated, both inwardly and outwardly.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it protrudes at the part where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is moved slightly.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is dislocated completely, you should make the patient sit upright, and hold their leg with force above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and place the foot in a nice manner up high; and do this twice, as we have said, by pulling and stretching the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, then begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place a strong stick firmly in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloth around so as not to hurt the patient; then hold the thigh with one person, and another person stretch the healthy leg with their hands or a strap, so that it is above the affected leg's ankle; then each person pulls equally, and the stick should be firmly between the patient's thighs to hold the patient in place when they are stretched; then put the dislocation back in its place with your hands, and another person holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, put the poultice and wadding on, and bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the heel, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if the bandage loosens, bind it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for 4 days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come (to the wound), you must calm them as we have said elsewhere until they are healed.[OP note: I'm assuming "covient" is a typo and should be "convient", which means "it is necessary". Please let me know if this is incorrect!]
des dois	of the shoulders
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any joint of the ankle, you should have the patient sit upright on a level surface or table, and place your foot on the visible joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns to its place; and when it is aligned and there is nothing apparent, place a two-chambered board under the sole of the foot, then bind it firmly and leave it for 3 days, then loosen it; and let the patient rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together[https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/ensamble](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/ensamble)
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with a dislocation, and one wants to restore it, it often happens that the patient dies; so do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, not hasty; and use at the beginning soothing remedies for the swollen abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the swelling comes to a head; and when the limb is in place, then administer soothing remedies for the swollen abscess, and treat the wound as it should be, with drying ointments; and if there is a fracture with the dislocation, and small bones are dislocated, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and be careful not to enter the path of fear, as I have said, for this will harm you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your art and your body.
Amen	 Amen
